<div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732491 id=\"55732491\" class=\"abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present spectroscopic confirmation of two new gravitationally lensed quasars, discovered in the Dark Energy Survey (DES) and <em>Wide-field Infrared Survey Explorer</em> (<em>WISE</em>) based on their multiband photometry and extended morphology in DES images. Images of DES J0115\u22125244 show a red galaxy with two blue point sources at either side, which are images of the same quasar at <em>z</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> = 1.64 as obtained by our long-slit spectroscopic data. The Einstein radius estimated from the DES images is 0.51 arcsec. DES J2146\u22120047 is in the area of overlap between DES and the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS). Two blue components are visible in the DES and SDSS images. The SDSS fibre spectrum shows a quasar component at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 2.38 and absorption by Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.799, which we tentatively associate with the foreground lens galaxy. Our long-slit spectra show that the blue components are resolved images of the same quasar. The Einstein radius is 0.68 arcsec, corresponding to an enclosed mass of 1.6 \u00d7 10<sup>11</sup> M<sub>\u022f</sub>. Three other candidates were observed and rejected, two being low-redshift pairs of starburst galaxies, and one being a quasar behind a blue star. These first confirmation results provide an important empirical validation of the data mining and model-based selection that is being applied to the entire DES data set.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: observational&quot;\">methods: observational</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: statistical&quot;\">methods: statistical</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;quasars: emission lines&quot;\">quasars: emission lines</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732493 id=\"55732493\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Gravitationally lensed quasars provide unique insights into a variety of fundamental open problems in cosmology and extragalactic astrophysics (e.g. Courbin, Saha &amp; Schechter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). When a quasar is strongly lensed by a galaxy, it results in multiple images of the same source, accompanied by arcs or rings that map the lensed host of the quasar. The light curves of different images are offset by a measurable time delay (e.g. Schechter et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1997</a>; Tewes et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) that depends on the cosmological distances to the lens and the source and the gravitational potential of the lens (Refsdal <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>). This enables one-step measurements of the expansion history of the Universe and the dark matter haloes of the massive galaxies that act as deflectors (e.g. Suyu et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). The microlensing effect on the multiple quasar images, induced by stars in the deflector, provides a quantitative handle on the stellar content of the lens galaxies (e.g. Schechter &amp; Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Oguri, Rusu &amp; Falco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Schechter et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Jim\u00e9nez-Vicente et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), and can simultaneously provide constraints on the inner structure of the lensed quasar, both the accretion disc size and the thermal profile (e.g. Anguita et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Eigenbrod et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Poindexter, Morgan &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Motta et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) as well as the geometry of the broad line region (e.g. Sluse et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29a\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29a\" data-open=\"bib29a\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Guerras et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12a\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12a\" data-open=\"bib12a\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Braibant et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4a\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4a\" data-open=\"bib4a\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Furthermore, millilensing via the so-called flux ratio anomalies provides a unique probe of the mass function of substructure and thus ultimately of the nature of dark matter (Mao &amp; Schneider <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Metcalf &amp; Madau <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>; Dalal &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Metcalf <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Nierenberg et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Finally, source reconstruction of the lensed quasar and its host give a direct view of quasar-host coevolution up to <em>z</em> \u223c 2 (Peng et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Rusu et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Advancement in the field is currently limited by the paucity of known systems suitable for detailed follow-up and analysis. A large sample of new systems will be transformative. To accomplish this, the STRIDES project,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>1</sup></a> a broad external collaboration of the Dark Energy Survey<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>2</sup></a> (DES, <a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://www.darkenergysurvey.org/index.shtml\" target=\"_blank\">http://www.darkenergysurvey.org/index.shtml</a>), aims at the discovery of the \u223c100 lensed quasars with primary image brighter than <em>i</em> = 21 mag predicted by Oguri &amp; Marshall (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) to lie within the DES footprint.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The identification of such rare systems over 5000 deg<sup>2</sup> of DES imaging data is a classic needle-in-a-haystack problem. The challenge is possibly greater than that faced in the SDSS data set (Oguri et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), as DES catalogues do not contain <em>u</em>-band data and there is no built-in spectroscopic data set to aid in the quasar selection. Fortunately, the DES image quality (median seeing \u223c0.9 arcsec) is better than that of SDSS, so one can rely on more accurate morphological information for candidate selection. New techniques have been developed in order to address this challenge (Agnello et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Chan et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we report on the first spectroscopic confirmation of lensed quasars from DES. We have obtained spectra of five of the 68 high-grade, small-separation candidate lensed quasars in the Year-1 DES data release footprint (hereafter Y1A1; Diehl et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), covering \u2248 1200 deg<sup>2</sup> in the Southern hemisphere.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This <em>Letter</em> is organized as follows. Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a> briefly illustrates the candidate-selection process and DES images of the two successful candidates from the first spectroscopic follow-up. Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> shows the long-slit spectroscopic data obtained for these systems. In Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>, we present the lensing properties that can be inferred with current data and conclude in Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>. Throughout this Letter, DES and <em>WISE</em> magnitudes are in the AB and Vega system, respectively. When needed in Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>, we adopt a concordance cosmology with \u03a9<sub>m</sub> = 0.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub> = 0.7, <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> = 70 km s<sup>\u2212 1</sup> Mpc<sup>\u2212 1</sup>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732499 id=\"55732499\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 QUASAR LENS CANDIDATE SELECTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We selected small-separation candidates from the DES Y1A1 data release, using a combination of colour cuts and data mining and model-based selection. Following Agnello et al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), we adopt a multistep strategy, whereby <em>targets</em> are first selected from catalogue data, and <em>candidates</em> are then selected from the targets by analysis of the actual multiband images. This multistep procedure allows one to keep the problem computationally fast.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732501 id=\"55732501\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>2.1 Preselection</h3>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Objects are preselected in the DES catalogue based on their \u2018blue\u2019 colours and extended morphology. The colour selection, satisfying <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\n&amp;&amp;{g-r&lt;0.6,\\ r-i&lt;0.45,\\ i-z&lt;0.55,}\\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{2.5&lt;i-W1&lt;5.5,\\ 0.7&lt;W1-W2&lt;2.0,}\\nonumber \\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{g-i&lt;1.2(i-W1)-2.8\\,,}\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>is only used to exclude the majority of galaxies and nearby blue stars from the pool being examined. Of these, we retain those satisfying <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ2\" content-id=\"equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\mathtt {psf{\\_}mag}-\\mathtt {model{\\_}mag}\\ge {\\rm dmag}\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>in DES <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em> bands simultaneously, with dmag = 0.125 in <em>g</em>, <em>r</em> bands and 0.2 in the <em>i</em> band. This ensures that the objects are not point-like (cf. Reed et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>, who use a similar but converse criterion for point-like objects).</div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Out of \u223c2 \u00d7 10<sup>5</sup> \u2018blue\u2019 systems, extended in the <em>i</em> band and with acceptable colours in DES <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> and <em>WISE W</em>1, <em>W</em>2 magnitudes, \u223c4000 are brighter than limiting magnitudes <em>i</em> = 21 or <em>W</em>1 = 17 and extended also in <em>g</em>, <em>r</em> bands.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732504 id=\"55732504\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2>2.2 Targets</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Of the 4000 blue extended objects, targets are selected by neural network classifiers (ANNs) based on their photometry and multiband morphology obtained at catalogue level. In particular, DES <span class=\"monospace\">model</span><em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> magnitudes and <em>WISE</em><span class=\"monospace\">w1mpro</span> (<em>W</em>1), <span class=\"monospace\">w2mpro</span> (<em>W</em>2) magnitudes are used for the photometry and DES model position angles and axis ratios in <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> are used for the morphology. ANNs produce membership probabilities for each object to belong to different classes, from which the targets are selected with cuts in output probabilities. The full procedure is discussed in detail by Agnello et al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). ANNs relying just on the photometry select 430 targets, out of which 136 are also selected by ANNs relying on multiband morphologies as well.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732506 id=\"55732506\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-3>2.3 Candidates</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The DES <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em>, <em>Y</em> image cutouts of selected targets have been modelled as combinations of point sources and galaxies to extract the SEDs of the extended and point sources. Based on the model results, we ranked candidates from \u20180\u2019 (not a lens) to \u20183\u2019 (good lens candidate), based on whether: (i) the point sources have consistent SEDs at least in <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> bands; (ii) their SEDs are compatible with those of quasars; (iii) the fainter quasar image is also redder in <em>g</em> \u2212 <em>r</em>; (iv) a possible lens galaxy is detected in the residuals or in <em>Y</em> band. At this stage, the selection shifts from automatic procedures (pre-selection, ANNs, modelling) to the investigator discretion, even though the ranking is based on the four quantitative criteria listed above. The final sample has 23 grade-\u20183\u2019 candidates and 45, 51, 17 with grades \u20182\u2019, \u20181\u2019, \u20180\u2019, respectively.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732508 id=\"55732508\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-4>2.4 First two confirmed lenses</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Fig. 1</a> shows DES multiband, single-epoch images in the best seeing conditions of the two successful candidates for which we describe spectroscopic follow-up in the next section. They are DES J0115\u22125244 at 01:15:57.32 \u221252:44:23.20 (top) and DES J2146\u22120047 at 21:46:46.04 \u221200:47:44.3 (bottom).</p>                        <a id=\"55732510\" scrollto-destination=\"55732510\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/m_stv2171fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&amp;Signature=LEY4eeqwJPVBhqTX0IjcMz1ChBJUr05BG8L~TK9peZaDADioh6ZTlrR0Dnrn16YrF3Fc-D9TlYYmh7GPP6TUrMpGkvO7HpU4qt5ccoUfLas2U~5CaAvmqROdPpq-vJ26EHrkWhFUiBBevGgyVAq2oVTODcFck-Alz-tx271z1Z6tWxcZaDI7v7HUaeM2khj5PKMcPTFV3aBItKQ9bSYwOCkuYJ91Nof0fuyS1fymA37wK5wiQMHt9V51caqSyCAXMvCzLA~-k4OKM-W5ydycDCVb-DZ4WRHVOK78lcULAPOapo2psiDUnrBAKroZgt6c~vthnQ59YKWCvZ1T38kBjQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"DES multiband single-epoch images with best seeing of DES J0115\u22125244 (top) and DES J2146\u22120047 (bottom), in 5 arcsec \u00d7 5 arcsec cutouts. North is up and east is left. From left to right, DES g, r, i, z, Y, and colour composites in gri, riz, izY.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig1.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/55732510/stv2171fig1.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig1.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"55732510\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/stv2171fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&Signature=COIqJjZSsZ06cUuVbvz45djeIo8RVok3MNTj0ASsCq99FURa-9TY7J0KRvWBQ7ot-LR~akdPY4mejYEHwKOl6~XBWRCbvtHnYEyfbJdg6RFitK8Cpry~7ZdwF1~voc5BfXGQjRx9yNKoyKygF3aLnpEqP0U6WYzm0VPaDh8ake1CTlqDeXLNHa3ABWIStrBsYHzwdzye85IpCBbrN04NBgijJGlbUp2~2XA51gEq0u~6PCZT86xpr5imw2ckQWN5yBBUL5sKwyNBL31T-Aceo7~REa4rcsJK-mtA-1l189tRdX895siQHkncoh7gXzhSJpX5kz0vBWnRHWwep169WQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=55732510&ar=2892767&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig1.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">DES multiband single-epoch images with best seeing of DES J0115\u22125244 (top) and DES J2146\u22120047 (bottom), in 5 arcsec \u00d7 5 arcsec cutouts. North is up and east is left. From left to right, DES <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em>, <em>Y</em>, and colour composites in <em>gri</em>, <em>riz</em>, <em>izY</em>.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The photometry and relative astrometry of the components in our composite models are summarized in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 1</a>. We have used the single-epoch DES cutouts with best image quality and adopted DES models of the PSF from nearby stars. For DES J2146\u22120047, we also fit Moffat profiles with the same structural parameters to each quasar image and a S\u00e9rsic profile to the lensing galaxy in archival Canada\u2013France\u2013Hawaii Telescope (CFHT) MegaCam <em>i</em>, <em>z</em>-band images (Programme 10BC22, PI: van Waerbeke). The resulting photometry is given in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 1</a> below the DES one. Even though the galaxy is below the detection limit in DES single-epoch data except in the <em>Y</em> band, it is securely detected in CFHT data in <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> bands as well.</p>                        <a id=\"55732512\" scrollto-destination=\"55732512\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Measured parameters of the systems in this Letter. The redshift of source <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> and lens <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> are obtained from our long-slit spectra and the SDSS public data. The relative astrometry and magnitudes of brighter (A) and fainter (B) quasar image and lens galaxy (G) are obtained by modelling the single-epoch DES images with best image quality (quoted under \u2018seeing FWHM\u2019). The right ascension (resp. declination) increases to the E (resp. to the N). Upper limits are given for magnitudes with \u22650.33 uncertainty. The galaxy in DES J2146\u22120047 is above the detection limit in DES <em>Y</em> band and in CFHT <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> bands. All quoted errors account for statistical uncertainties from cutout fitting an not e.g. possible systematics from PSF mismatch.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>Syst.<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>z</em><sub>s</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>z</em><sub>l</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>\u0394RA (arcsec)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>\u0394Dec. arcsec\u00a0</td><td>0.87 arcsec\u00a0</td><td>0.82 arcsec\u00a0</td><td>0.77 arcsec\u00a0</td><td>1.26 arcsec\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>DES <span class=\"monospace\">model</span>\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>19.52\u00a0</td><td>19.67\u00a0</td><td>19.48\u00a0</td><td>19.16\u00a0</td><td>19.05\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/55732512\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Three additional candidates have been observed during the same observing run and ruled out as lensed quasars. They are briefly described in Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3.3</a> below.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732514 id=\"55732514\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 SPECTROSCOPIC CONFIRMATION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Spectra were obtained with the Inamori Magellan Areal Camera and Spectrograph (IMACS; Dressler et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) on the Baade 6.5-m telescope on <span class=\"small-caps\">ut</span> 2015 June 19. The f/4 camera was used with 0.70 \u2212 arcsec slit mask. The data were binned factors of 2 along the slit, giving a scale of 0.22 arcsec pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>, and 4 in the spectral direction, which combined with a 300 l mm<sup>\u22121</sup> grating gave a dispersion of 2.92 \u00c5 pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>. Two CCDs covered the spectra over 3770\u20135260 \u00c5 and 5350\u20136880 \u00c5. The seeing ranged between 0.8 and 1.2 arcsec, and all our candidates were partially or completely resolved. Two spectra of 600 s were taken for each object. The data were reduced using standard <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> routines.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">One-dimensional (1D) spectra have been extracted by modelling the 2D spectra as superpositions of Gaussian tracks in the spatial dimension, one per component, having peak positions (<em>p</em><sub>1</sub>, <em>p</em><sub>2</sub>) that are linear functions of the wavelength with the same slope (d<em>p</em>/d\u03bb). Even though the individual tracks are generally well separated, this procedure ensures that the resulting 1D spectra are as independent as possible from one another and exploit all the information available in the 2D tracks.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Five grade-\u20183\u2019 candidates were visible and observed. The resulting spectra are described below. The results on the two confirmed lenses are shown in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Fig. 2</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"55732518\" scrollto-destination=\"55732518\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/m_stv2171fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&amp;Signature=OoLq8b1L5-7sA73Kzio4JC5oAIIjH8jdAhSSOJ0VLgkm52-r0Rqo~CyzL6jy37UaZli-e~rusbFYXeJnNOjojpH2EL7m9oc5wPaDPXHe1UwL54mHDoy1acPFES8QdzauWT5TOW8AKsgsvjESX78KnNnijGhCTexdWVA3N7rXTNsFq-ck7RFcvk8exzL1wpI6nMdDgc1-qai~tO~5YTKlunlsAXZkjjL35TaGOj9vu5G9d6hOeCsV24EWH~VgEiDe~IY9qkOjUUdkvUFZzmGOsUCPEstW40BXmjqX8TNJII~woj5CNaNsNbGdGdQkTxLRDGVn4JncHTmEliqTJaW5eg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"1D sky-subtracted spectra of DES J0115\u22125244 (left) and DES J2146\u22120047 (right). The red and blue histograms show the spectra of the two components, demonstrating that they are images of the same quasar. Emission and absorption lines are marked by blue (solid) and red (dashed) vertical lines, respectively.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/m_stv2171fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&amp;Signature=OoLq8b1L5-7sA73Kzio4JC5oAIIjH8jdAhSSOJ0VLgkm52-r0Rqo~CyzL6jy37UaZli-e~rusbFYXeJnNOjojpH2EL7m9oc5wPaDPXHe1UwL54mHDoy1acPFES8QdzauWT5TOW8AKsgsvjESX78KnNnijGhCTexdWVA3N7rXTNsFq-ck7RFcvk8exzL1wpI6nMdDgc1-qai~tO~5YTKlunlsAXZkjjL35TaGOj9vu5G9d6hOeCsV24EWH~VgEiDe~IY9qkOjUUdkvUFZzmGOsUCPEstW40BXmjqX8TNJII~woj5CNaNsNbGdGdQkTxLRDGVn4JncHTmEliqTJaW5eg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"1D sky-subtracted spectra of DES J0115\u22125244 (left) and DES J2146\u22120047 (right). Emission and absorption lines are marked by blue (solid) and red (dashed) vertical lines, respectively.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig2.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/55732518/stv2171fig2.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig2.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"55732518\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/stv2171fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&Signature=k0AUhh0Jdyl85RamcmiRWXf6ZCtFoH6nFQjh-wQM6nVRXjRP6u7JbEdZGUM0FhF8IFJoiYJhSuaGpbbgOFQJ8KLAgkDqquEXiCspJILtywhBZ-c61TX66cTEDvgMaUrlT5WLGbc8CRBVHwdfSUIkDbCHPEk1fXW0QTlOzVOQdFztcCVzg3T~yS9QV~d~ABCqJTE6Zv0MQEAPXmBIJk7os-iQyvVHC7QihDjw7y9byP0WK~QTn6LQYPBHnS964rO9CPjvhU~TsG8QGs9wrCnrZstqShHJe1D4qUcIEnJ8k-whggROS~wxrMRHB-miAENJBZ56MH7IsgymskoJA1Kmmw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=55732518&ar=2892767&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig2.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">1D sky-subtracted spectra of DES J0115\u22125244 (left) and DES J2146\u22120047 (right). The red and blue histograms show the spectra of the two components, demonstrating that they are images of the same quasar. Emission and absorption lines are marked by blue (solid) and red (dashed) vertical lines, respectively.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732519 id=\"55732519\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-1>3.1 DES J0115\u22125244</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The 1D spectra of DES J0115\u22125244 show the same broad emission lines (C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, He <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]) at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 1.64, with a uniform ratio between the two spectra in the red, as shown in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Fig. 2</a>, indicating that the low-order differences between the two spectra are due to differential reddening, or perhaps chromatic microlensing. Together with the presence of a red galaxy in the DES images, the spectra confirm DES J0115\u22125244 as a strongly lensed quasar, with image separation \u22481.04 arcsec. Unfortunately, the S/N ratio is too low to securely detect stellar absorption lines from the deflector.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732521 id=\"55732521\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-2>3.2 DES J2146\u22120047</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The 1D spectra of DES J2146\u22120047 show two components with the same broad emission lines at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 2.38, consistent with the public SDSS fibre spectrum. Prominent Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> absorption lines at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.799 are detected in both spectra (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Fig. 2</a>). The ratio between the two spectra is constant, which together with the detection of a galaxy in <em>izY</em> bands confirms DES J2146\u22120047 as a strongly lensed quasar, with image separation \u22481.32 arcsec. We associate the lens redshift with the galaxy responsible for the absorption lines at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>. This system has been independently identified as part of the SDSS-III quasar lens sample (More et al., in preparation).</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732523 id=\"55732523\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-3>3.3 False positives</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Two candidates, at 20:53:56.5 \u221256:09:36 and 22:17:52.5 \u221253:57:15, respectively, are pairs of compact, star-forming galaxies. The third rejected candidate, at 22:00:24.11 +01:10:37.56, is an alignment of a <em>z</em> = 1.37 red quasar and a blue star, with the same <em>r</em> \u2212 <em>i</em> and <em>i</em> \u2212 <em>z</em> colours by coincidence.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In general, pairs of compact star forming galaxies at <em>z</em> \u2248 0.2\u20130.3 are the main residual contaminant from the candidate-selection procedure, because their broad-band colours are consistent with those of quasars. This includes initial candidates that we rejected based on their available SDSS spectra. In <em>WISE</em> magnitudes, they tend to lie at <em>W</em>2 &gt; 14 and <em>W</em>1 \u2212 <em>W</em>2 &lt; 0.8, across the limiting locus of Assef et al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), a region that however is occupied also by spectroscopicallyconfirmed quasars and some of the candidates from this search.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732526 id=\"55732526\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 LENSING PROPERTIES</h2>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Even though the current data are not sufficient for a detailed lensing model, they can be used to derive simple properties of the lens galaxies. To this aim, we adopt a Singular Isothermal Sphere (SIS) model for the mass density profile of the deflector, which is commonly considered the simplest model apt to describe galaxy-scale lenses (Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). The SIS projected surface density is <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ3\" content-id=\"equ3\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\Sigma (R)=\\frac{1}{2}\\Sigma _{cr}(R/R_{\\mathrm{E}})^{-1}\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(3)</span></div>with \u03a3<sub>cr</sub> = <em>c</em><sup>2</sup><em>D</em><sub>s</sub>/(4\u03c0<em>GD</em><sub>l</sub><em>D</em><sub>ls</sub>) in terms of angular diameter distances to the source (<em>D</em><sub>s</sub>), to the lens (<em>D</em><sub>l</sub>) and between lens and source (<em>D</em><sub>ls</sub>), and the Einstein radius <em>R</em><sub>E</sub> is defined such that it encloses a projected mass <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ4\" content-id=\"equ4\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\nM_{\\rm E}\\ =\\ \\pi \\Sigma _{\\rm {cr}}R_{\\mathrm{E}}^{2}\\ .\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(4)</span></div>The expected line-of-sight velocity dispersion of stars in the lens galaxy can be estimated via <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ5\" content-id=\"equ5\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\sigma ^{2}_{\\rm {sis}}=\\frac{c^{2}R_{\\mathrm{E}}D_{\\rm s}}{4\\pi D_{\\rm l}D_{\\rm {ls}}}\\ .\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(5)</span></div>Finally, neglecting microlensing, the total magnification of the point source can be estimated from the flux ratio <em>f</em><sub><em>B</em></sub>/<em>f</em><sub><em>A</em></sub> as <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ6\" content-id=\"equ6\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\mu _{\\rm {tot}}=2\\frac{1+f_{B}/f_{A}}{1-f_{B}/f_{A}}\\,,\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(6)</span></div>where A is the brighter quasar image. Then, from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 1</a> and confirmation spectra, we can estimate <em>R</em><sub>E</sub>, <em>M</em><sub>E</sub>, \u03c3<sub>sis</sub> and \u03bc<sub>tot</sub>. The Einstein radius is approximated by half the image separation (an exact result for SIS profiles). For the flux ratio, we use the average between <em>i</em> and <em>z</em> bands, for which the photometric fit is more robust against PSF mismatch and signal-to-noise ratio(S/N), and the effects of dust and microlensing are minimized. The results are summarized in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 2</a>. For DES J0115\u22125244, we adopted a lens redshift <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.635, which minimizes the critical surface density \u03a3<sub>cr</sub> and yields a lower bound on \u03c3<sub>sis</sub>. We also list the magnification inferred from the ratio of continua in the spectra around 6000 \u00c5. With the positional uncertainties from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 1</a>, the relative uncertainty on <em>R</em><sub>E</sub> is 1\u2009per\u2009cent. With current data, the uncertainties on the magnifications are of the same order as their average value.</div>                        <a id=\"55732528\" scrollto-destination=\"55732528\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl2\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl2\" data-id=\"tbl2\"><span class=\"label\">Table 2.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Estimated lensing parameters and properties of the lens galaxy: Einstein radius <em>R</em><sub>E</sub> (in angular units) and total magnification \u03bc<sub>tot, <em>i</em></sub> from the fit to the quasar image positions and fluxes; magnification \u03bc<sub>tot, <em>c</em></sub> on the quasar continua, from the 1D spectra; and SIS velocity dipersion \u03c3<sub>sis</sub> and enclosed mass <em>M</em><sub>E</sub> from the measured redshifts. For DES J0115\u22125244, \u03c3<sub>sis</sub> and <em>M</em><sub>E</sub> are under the hypothesis that the lens is midway between observer and source (i.e. <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.635).</p></div> href=\"/view-large/55732528\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732529 id=\"55732529\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have presented the very first results of a campaign to extend the known samples of lensed quasars by exploiting the large footprint of wide-field photometric surveys. In particular, we have spectroscopically confirmed two new systems, found in the DES Y1A1 release with data-mining techniques. Two additional candidates were ruled out by spectroscopic observations as pairs of <em>z</em> \u2248 0.2 compact, narrow-line galaxies. Another candidate was ruled out as an alignment of a quasar and a blue star. The basic characteristics of the two confirmed systems are as follows.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>DES J0115\u22125244.</em> Consists of two images of a quasar at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 1.64 lensed by a foreground galaxy visible in the DES images. No redshift is available for the lens galaxy. The Einstein Radius is estimated to be 0.51 arcsec.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>DES J2146\u22120047.</em> Consists of two images of a quasar at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 2.38, with prominent Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> absorption at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.799, which we tentatively associate with the lens galaxy redshift. The redshift of the lensing galaxy is not confirmed in the spectroscopic follow-up by More et al. (in preparation), since detection of the Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> lines depends on S/N ratio and in fact is less evident in the worse of our two exposures, where track deconvolution becomes more noisy. Thus, deeper spectroscopic data will be needed to measure the redshift of the deflector, possibly based on stellar absorption lines. The Einstein Radius is estimated to be 0.68 arcsec.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The main class of contaminants (including candidates rejected based on their SDSS spectra) consists of groups of compact, star-forming galaxies at <em>z</em> \u223c 0.2\u20130.3, because of their broad-band colours and compact morphology. With the observed sample, a strict cut in <em>WISE W</em>1 \u2212 <em>W</em>2 versus <em>W</em>2 would give a 100 per cent success rate, which drops at 40 per cent when the cut is relaxed. Still, with just five systems currently at hand, we would rather caution against these simple estimates.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Our search has delivered over 100 additional candidates from the Y1A1 data \u2013 and we expect many more from the next seasons of DES data. The results of this first follow-up effort are encouraging. However, a systematic follow-up campaign is needed to confirm large numbers of candidates, assess the purity of our selection technique, and carry out the many scientific investigations enabled by lensed quasars.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732535 id=\"55732535\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >ACKNOWLEDGMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">This Letter includes data gathered with the 6.5m Baade Telescopes located at Las Campanas Observatory, Chile. The redshift of source <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> and lens <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> are obtained from our long-slit spectra and the SDSS public data. The relative astrometry and magnitudes of brighter (A) and fainter (B) quasar image and lens galaxy (G) are obtained by modelling the single-epoch DES images with best image quality (quoted under \u2018seeing FWHM\u2019). The right ascension (resp. declination) increases to the E (resp. to the N). Upper limits are given for magnitudes with \u22650.33 uncertainty. The galaxy in DES J2146\u22120047 is above the detection limit in DES <em>Y</em> band and in CFHT <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> bands. The galaxy in DES J2146\u22120047 is above the detection limit in DES <em>Y</em> band and in CFHT <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> bands. <div class=\"widget widget-ArticleFulltext widget-instance-OUP_Article_FullText_Widget\">\n        <div class=\"module-widget\">\r\n    <div class=\"widget-items\" data-widgetname=\"ArticleFulltext\">\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n\r\n                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732491 id=\"55732491\" class=\"abstract-title\" >ABSTRACT</h2>\r\n<section class=\"abstract\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">We present spectroscopic confirmation of two new gravitationally lensed quasars, discovered in the Dark Energy Survey (DES) and <em>Wide-field Infrared Survey Explorer</em> (<em>WISE</em>) based on their multiband photometry and extended morphology in DES images. Images of DES J0115\u22125244 show a red galaxy with two blue point sources at either side, which are images of the same quasar at <em>z</em><sub><em>s</em></sub> = 1.64 as obtained by our long-slit spectroscopic data. The Einstein radius estimated from the DES images is 0.51 arcsec. DES J2146\u22120047 is in the area of overlap between DES and the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS). Two blue components are visible in the DES and SDSS images. The SDSS fibre spectrum shows a quasar component at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 2.38 and absorption by Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.799, which we tentatively associate with the foreground lens galaxy. Our long-slit spectra show that the blue components are resolved images of the same quasar. The Einstein radius is 0.68 arcsec, corresponding to an enclosed mass of 1.6 \u00d7 10<sup>11</sup> M<sub>\u022f</sub>. Three other candidates were observed and rejected, two being low-redshift pairs of starburst galaxies, and one being a quasar behind a blue star. These first confirmation results provide an important empirical validation of the data mining and model-based selection that is being applied to the entire DES data set.</p></section>                        <div class=\"article-metadata-panel clearfix\"></div>\r\n<div class=\"kwd-group\"><a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;gravitational lensing: strong&quot;\">gravitational lensing: strong</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: observational&quot;\">methods: observational</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;methods: statistical&quot;\">methods: statistical</a>, <a class=\"kwd-part kwd-main\" href=\"javascript:;\" data-keyword=\"&quot;quasars: emission lines&quot;\">quasars: emission lines</a></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732493 id=\"55732493\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec1>1 INTRODUCTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Gravitationally lensed quasars provide unique insights into a variety of fundamental open problems in cosmology and extragalactic astrophysics (e.g. Courbin, Saha &amp; Schechter <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib5\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib5\" data-open=\"bib5\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>). When a quasar is strongly lensed by a galaxy, it results in multiple images of the same source, accompanied by arcs or rings that map the lensed host of the quasar. The light curves of different images are offset by a measurable time delay (e.g. Schechter et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib27\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib27\" data-open=\"bib27\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1997</a>; Tewes et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib30\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib30\" data-open=\"bib30\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>) that depends on the cosmological distances to the lens and the source and the gravitational potential of the lens (Refsdal <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib24\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib24\" data-open=\"bib24\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1964</a>). This enables one-step measurements of the expansion history of the Universe and the dark matter haloes of the massive galaxies that act as deflectors (e.g. Suyu et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29\" data-open=\"bib29\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). The microlensing effect on the multiple quasar images, induced by stars in the deflector, provides a quantitative handle on the stellar content of the lens galaxies (e.g. Schechter &amp; Wambsganss <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib26\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib26\" data-open=\"bib26\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Oguri, Rusu &amp; Falco <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib20\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib20\" data-open=\"bib20\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Schechter et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib28\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib28\" data-open=\"bib28\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>; Jim\u00e9nez-Vicente et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12\" data-open=\"bib12\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), and can simultaneously provide constraints on the inner structure of the lensed quasar, both the accretion disc size and the thermal profile (e.g. Anguita et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib2\" data-open=\"bib2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Eigenbrod et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib9\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib9\" data-open=\"bib9\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Poindexter, Morgan &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib22\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib22\" data-open=\"bib22\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>; Motta et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib16\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib16\" data-open=\"bib16\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2012</a>) as well as the geometry of the broad line region (e.g. Sluse et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib29a\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib29a\" data-open=\"bib29a\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>; Guerras et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib12a\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib12a\" data-open=\"bib12a\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>; Braibant et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4a\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4a\" data-open=\"bib4a\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Furthermore, millilensing via the so-called flux ratio anomalies provides a unique probe of the mass function of substructure and thus ultimately of the nature of dark matter (Mao &amp; Schneider <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib13\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib13\" data-open=\"bib13\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">1998</a>; Metcalf &amp; Madau <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib15\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib15\" data-open=\"bib15\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2001</a>; Dalal &amp; Kochanek <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib6\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib6\" data-open=\"bib6\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Metcalf <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib14\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib14\" data-open=\"bib14\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2002</a>; Nierenberg et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib17\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib17\" data-open=\"bib17\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>). Finally, source reconstruction of the lensed quasar and its host give a direct view of quasar-host coevolution up to <em>z</em> \u223c 2 (Peng et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib21\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib21\" data-open=\"bib21\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Rusu et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib25\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib25\" data-open=\"bib25\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Advancement in the field is currently limited by the paucity of known systems suitable for detailed follow-up and analysis. A large sample of new systems will be transformative. To accomplish this, the STRIDES project,<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn1\" data-open=\"fn1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>1</sup></a> a broad external collaboration of the Dark Energy Survey<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fn2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fn2\" data-open=\"fn2\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-fn js-xref-fn\"><sup>2</sup></a> (DES, <a class=\"link link-uri openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"http://www.darkenergysurvey.org/index.shtml\" target=\"_blank\">http://www.darkenergysurvey.org/index.shtml</a>), aims at the discovery of the \u223c100 lensed quasars with primary image brighter than <em>i</em> = 21 mag predicted by Oguri &amp; Marshall (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib18\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib18\" data-open=\"bib18\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>) to lie within the DES footprint.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The identification of such rare systems over 5000 deg<sup>2</sup> of DES imaging data is a classic needle-in-a-haystack problem. The challenge is possibly greater than that faced in the SDSS data set (Oguri et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib19\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib19\" data-open=\"bib19\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2006</a>; Inada et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib11\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib11\" data-open=\"bib11\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2008</a>), as DES catalogues do not contain <em>u</em>-band data and there is no built-in spectroscopic data set to aid in the quasar selection. Fortunately, the DES image quality (median seeing \u223c0.9 arcsec) is better than that of SDSS, so one can rely on more accurate morphological information for candidate selection. New techniques have been developed in order to address this challenge (Agnello et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>; Chan et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib4\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib4\" data-open=\"bib4\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>).</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Here, we report on the first spectroscopic confirmation of lensed quasars from DES. We have obtained spectra of five of the 68 high-grade, small-separation candidate lensed quasars in the Year-1 DES data release footprint (hereafter Y1A1; Diehl et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib7\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib7\" data-open=\"bib7\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2014</a>), covering \u2248 1200 deg<sup>2</sup> in the Southern hemisphere.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">This <em>Letter</em> is organized as follows. Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec2\"></span><a href=\"#sec2\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">2</a> briefly illustrates the candidate-selection process and DES images of the two successful candidates from the first spectroscopic follow-up. Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3</a> shows the long-slit spectroscopic data obtained for these systems. In Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>, we present the lensing properties that can be inferred with current data and conclude in Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec5\"></span><a href=\"#sec5\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">5</a>. Throughout this Letter, DES and <em>WISE</em> magnitudes are in the AB and Vega system, respectively. When needed in Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec4\"></span><a href=\"#sec4\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">4</a>, we adopt a concordance cosmology with \u03a9<sub>m</sub> = 0.3, \u03a9<sub>\u039b</sub> = 0.7, <em>H</em><sub>0</sub> = 70 km s<sup>\u2212 1</sup> Mpc<sup>\u2212 1</sup>.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732499 id=\"55732499\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2>2 QUASAR LENS CANDIDATE SELECTION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We selected small-separation candidates from the DES Y1A1 data release, using a combination of colour cuts and data mining and model-based selection. Following Agnello et al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>), we adopt a multistep strategy, whereby <em>targets</em> are first selected from catalogue data, and <em>candidates</em> are then selected from the targets by analysis of the actual multiband images. This multistep procedure allows one to keep the problem computationally fast.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732501 id=\"55732501\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-1>2.1 Preselection</h3>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Objects are preselected in the DES catalogue based on their \u2018blue\u2019 colours and extended morphology. The colour selection, satisfying <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ1\" content-id=\"equ1\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{eqnarray}\r\n&amp;&amp;{g-r&lt;0.6,\\ r-i&lt;0.45,\\ i-z&lt;0.55,}\\nonumber\\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{2.5&lt;i-W1&lt;5.5,\\ 0.7&lt;W1-W2&lt;2.0,}\\nonumber \\\\\r\n&amp;&amp;{g-i&lt;1.2(i-W1)-2.8\\,,}\r\n\\end{eqnarray} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(1)</span></div>is only used to exclude the majority of galaxies and nearby blue stars from the pool being examined. Of these, we retain those satisfying <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ2\" content-id=\"equ2\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\mathtt {psf{\\_}mag}-\\mathtt {model{\\_}mag}\\ge {\\rm dmag}\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(2)</span></div>in DES <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em> bands simultaneously, with dmag = 0.125 in <em>g</em>, <em>r</em> bands and 0.2 in the <em>i</em> band. This ensures that the objects are not point-like (cf. Reed et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib23\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib23\" data-open=\"bib23\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>, who use a similar but converse criterion for point-like objects).</div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Out of \u223c2 \u00d7 10<sup>5</sup> \u2018blue\u2019 systems, extended in the <em>i</em> band and with acceptable colours in DES <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> and <em>WISE W</em>1, <em>W</em>2 magnitudes, \u223c4000 are brighter than limiting magnitudes <em>i</em> = 21 or <em>W</em>1 = 17 and extended also in <em>g</em>, <em>r</em> bands.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732504 id=\"55732504\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-2>2.2 Targets</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Of the 4000 blue extended objects, targets are selected by neural network classifiers (ANNs) based on their photometry and multiband morphology obtained at catalogue level. In particular, DES <span class=\"monospace\">model</span><em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> magnitudes and <em>WISE</em><span class=\"monospace\">w1mpro</span> (<em>W</em>1), <span class=\"monospace\">w2mpro</span> (<em>W</em>2) magnitudes are used for the photometry and DES model position angles and axis ratios in <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> are used for the morphology. ANNs produce membership probabilities for each object to belong to different classes, from which the targets are selected with cuts in output probabilities. The full procedure is discussed in detail by Agnello et al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib1\" data-open=\"bib1\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2015</a>). ANNs relying just on the photometry select 430 targets, out of which 136 are also selected by ANNs relying on multiband morphologies as well.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732506 id=\"55732506\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-3>2.3 Candidates</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The DES <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em>, <em>Y</em> image cutouts of selected targets have been modelled as combinations of point sources and galaxies to extract the SEDs of the extended and point sources. Based on the model results, we ranked candidates from \u20180\u2019 (not a lens) to \u20183\u2019 (good lens candidate), based on whether: (i) the point sources have consistent SEDs at least in <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> bands; (ii) their SEDs are compatible with those of quasars; (iii) the fainter quasar image is also redder in <em>g</em> \u2212 <em>r</em>; (iv) a possible lens galaxy is detected in the residuals or in <em>Y</em> band. At this stage, the selection shifts from automatic procedures (pre-selection, ANNs, modelling) to the investigator discretion, even though the ranking is based on the four quantitative criteria listed above. The final sample has 23 grade-\u20183\u2019 candidates and 45, 51, 17 with grades \u20182\u2019, \u20181\u2019, \u20180\u2019, respectively.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732508 id=\"55732508\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec2-4>2.4 First two confirmed lenses</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\"><span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig1\" data-open=\"fig1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Fig. 1</a> shows DES multiband, single-epoch images in the best seeing conditions of the two successful candidates for which we describe spectroscopic follow-up in the next section. They are DES J0115\u22125244 at 01:15:57.32 \u221252:44:23.20 (top) and DES J2146\u22120047 at 21:46:46.04 \u221200:47:44.3 (bottom).</p>                        <a id=\"55732510\" scrollto-destination=\"55732510\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig1\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 1.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/m_stv2171fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&amp;Signature=LEY4eeqwJPVBhqTX0IjcMz1ChBJUr05BG8L~TK9peZaDADioh6ZTlrR0Dnrn16YrF3Fc-D9TlYYmh7GPP6TUrMpGkvO7HpU4qt5ccoUfLas2U~5CaAvmqROdPpq-vJ26EHrkWhFUiBBevGgyVAq2oVTODcFck-Alz-tx271z1Z6tWxcZaDI7v7HUaeM2khj5PKMcPTFV3aBItKQ9bSYwOCkuYJ91Nof0fuyS1fymA37wK5wiQMHt9V51caqSyCAXMvCzLA~-k4OKM-W5ydycDCVb-DZ4WRHVOK78lcULAPOapo2psiDUnrBAKroZgt6c~vthnQ59YKWCvZ1T38kBjQ__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"DES multiband single-epoch images with best seeing of DES J0115\u22125244 (top) and DES J2146\u22120047 (bottom), in 5 arcsec \u00d7 5 arcsec cutouts. North is up and east is left. From left to right, DES g, r, i, z, Y, and colour composites in gri, riz, izY.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig1.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/55732510/stv2171fig1.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig1.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"55732510\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/stv2171fig1.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&Signature=COIqJjZSsZ06cUuVbvz45djeIo8RVok3MNTj0ASsCq99FURa-9TY7J0KRvWBQ7ot-LR~akdPY4mejYEHwKOl6~XBWRCbvtHnYEyfbJdg6RFitK8Cpry~7ZdwF1~voc5BfXGQjRx9yNKoyKygF3aLnpEqP0U6WYzm0VPaDh8ake1CTlqDeXLNHa3ABWIStrBsYHzwdzye85IpCBbrN04NBgijJGlbUp2~2XA51gEq0u~6PCZT86xpr5imw2ckQWN5yBBUL5sKwyNBL31T-Aceo7~REa4rcsJK-mtA-1l189tRdX895siQHkncoh7gXzhSJpX5kz0vBWnRHWwep169WQ__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=55732510&ar=2892767&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig1.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">DES multiband single-epoch images with best seeing of DES J0115\u22125244 (top) and DES J2146\u22120047 (bottom), in 5 arcsec \u00d7 5 arcsec cutouts. North is up and east is left. From left to right, DES <em>g</em>, <em>r</em>, <em>i</em>, <em>z</em>, <em>Y</em>, and colour composites in <em>gri</em>, <em>riz</em>, <em>izY</em>.</p></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">The photometry and relative astrometry of the components in our composite models are summarized in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 1</a>. We have used the single-epoch DES cutouts with best image quality and adopted DES models of the PSF from nearby stars. For DES J2146\u22120047, we also fit Moffat profiles with the same structural parameters to each quasar image and a S\u00e9rsic profile to the lensing galaxy in archival Canada\u2013France\u2013Hawaii Telescope (CFHT) MegaCam <em>i</em>, <em>z</em>-band images (Programme 10BC22, PI: van Waerbeke). The resulting photometry is given in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 1</a> below the DES one. Even though the galaxy is below the detection limit in DES single-epoch data except in the <em>Y</em> band, it is securely detected in CFHT data in <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> bands as well.</p>                        <a id=\"55732512\" scrollto-destination=\"55732512\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl1\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl1\" data-id=\"tbl1\"><span class=\"label\">Table 1.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Measured parameters of the systems in this Letter. The redshift of source <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> and lens <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> are obtained from our long-slit spectra and the SDSS public data. The relative astrometry and magnitudes of brighter (A) and fainter (B) quasar image and lens galaxy (G) are obtained by modelling the single-epoch DES images with best image quality (quoted under \u2018seeing FWHM\u2019). The right ascension (resp. declination) increases to the E (resp. to the N). Upper limits are given for magnitudes with \u22650.33 uncertainty. The galaxy in DES J2146\u22120047 is above the detection limit in DES <em>Y</em> band and in CFHT <em>i</em>, <em>z</em> bands. All quoted errors account for statistical uncertainties from cutout fitting an not e.g. possible systematics from PSF mismatch.</p></div> </div><div class=\"table-overflow\"><table><thead><tr><th>Syst.<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>z</em><sub>s</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th><em>z</em><sub>l</sub><span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>\u0394RA (arcsec)<span aria-hidden=\"true\" style=\"display: none;\">\r\n            .\u00a0</span></th><th>\u0394Dec. arcsec\u00a0</td><td>0.87 arcsec\u00a0</td><td>0.82 arcsec\u00a0</td><td>0.77 arcsec\u00a0</td><td>1.26 arcsec\u00a0</td></tr><tr><td>DES <span class=\"monospace\">model</span>\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>\u2013\u00a0</td><td>19.52\u00a0</td><td>19.67\u00a0</td><td>19.48\u00a0</td><td>19.16\u00a0</td><td>19.05\u00a0</td></tr></tbody></table></div><div class=\"&#xA;          graphic-wrap&#xA;          \"><a class=\"fig-view-orig openInAnotherWindow btn js-view-large\" target=\"_blank\" href=\"/view-large/55732512\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div><p class=\"chapter-para\">Three additional candidates have been observed during the same observing run and ruled out as lensed quasars. They are briefly described in Section <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-sec3-3\"></span><a href=\"#sec3-3\" class=\"sectionLink xref-sec\">3.3</a> below.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732514 id=\"55732514\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3>3 SPECTROSCOPIC CONFIRMATION</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Spectra were obtained with the Inamori Magellan Areal Camera and Spectrograph (IMACS; Dressler et al. <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib8\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib8\" data-open=\"bib8\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2011</a>) on the Baade 6.5-m telescope on <span class=\"small-caps\">ut</span> 2015 June 19. The f/4 camera was used with 0.70 \u2212 arcsec slit mask. The data were binned factors of 2 along the slit, giving a scale of 0.22 arcsec pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>, and 4 in the spectral direction, which combined with a 300 l mm<sup>\u22121</sup> grating gave a dispersion of 2.92 \u00c5 pixel<sup>\u22121</sup>. Two CCDs covered the spectra over 3770\u20135260 \u00c5 and 5350\u20136880 \u00c5. The seeing ranged between 0.8 and 1.2 arcsec, and all our candidates were partially or completely resolved. Two spectra of 600 s were taken for each object. The data were reduced using standard <span class=\"small-caps\">iraf</span> routines.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">One-dimensional (1D) spectra have been extracted by modelling the 2D spectra as superpositions of Gaussian tracks in the spatial dimension, one per component, having peak positions (<em>p</em><sub>1</sub>, <em>p</em><sub>2</sub>) that are linear functions of the wavelength with the same slope (d<em>p</em>/d\u03bb). Even though the individual tracks are generally well separated, this procedure ensures that the resulting 1D spectra are as independent as possible from one another and exploit all the information available in the 2D tracks.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Five grade-\u20183\u2019 candidates were visible and observed. The resulting spectra are described below. The results on the two confirmed lenses are shown in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Fig. 2</a>.</p>                        <a id=\"55732518\" scrollto-destination=\"55732518\"></a>\r\n<div data-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-section js-fig-section\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/m_stv2171fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&amp;Signature=OoLq8b1L5-7sA73Kzio4JC5oAIIjH8jdAhSSOJ0VLgkm52-r0Rqo~CyzL6jy37UaZli-e~rusbFYXeJnNOjojpH2EL7m9oc5wPaDPXHe1UwL54mHDoy1acPFES8QdzauWT5TOW8AKsgsvjESX78KnNnijGhCTexdWVA3N7rXTNsFq-ck7RFcvk8exzL1wpI6nMdDgc1-qai~tO~5YTKlunlsAXZkjjL35TaGOj9vu5G9d6hOeCsV24EWH~VgEiDe~IY9qkOjUUdkvUFZzmGOsUCPEstW40BXmjqX8TNJII~woj5CNaNsNbGdGdQkTxLRDGVn4JncHTmEliqTJaW5eg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"1D sky-subtracted spectra of DES J0115\u22125244 (left) and DES J2146\u22120047 (right). The red and blue histograms show the spectra of the two components, demonstrating that they are images of the same quasar. Emission and absorption lines are marked by blue (solid) and red (dashed) vertical lines, respectively.</p></div></div><div content-id=\"fig2\" class=\"fig fig-modal reveal-modal\"><div class=\"label fig-label\">Figure 2.</div><div class=\"graphic-wrap\"><img class=\"content-image\" src=\"https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/m_stv2171fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&amp;Signature=OoLq8b1L5-7sA73Kzio4JC5oAIIjH8jdAhSSOJ0VLgkm52-r0Rqo~CyzL6jy37UaZli-e~rusbFYXeJnNOjojpH2EL7m9oc5wPaDPXHe1UwL54mHDoy1acPFES8QdzauWT5TOW8AKsgsvjESX78KnNnijGhCTexdWVA3N7rXTNsFq-ck7RFcvk8exzL1wpI6nMdDgc1-qai~tO~5YTKlunlsAXZkjjL35TaGOj9vu5G9d6hOeCsV24EWH~VgEiDe~IY9qkOjUUdkvUFZzmGOsUCPEstW40BXmjqX8TNJII~woj5CNaNsNbGdGdQkTxLRDGVn4JncHTmEliqTJaW5eg__&amp;Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA\" alt=\"1D sky-subtracted spectra of DES J0115\u22125244 (left) and DES J2146\u22120047 (right).
