Emission and absorption lines are marked by blue (solid) and red (dashed) vertical lines, respectively.\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig2.jpeg\" /><div class=\"fig-orig original-slide\"><a class=\"fig-view-orig js-view-large openInAnotherWindow\" href=\"/view-large/figure/55732518/stv2171fig2.jpeg\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig2.jpeg\" target=\"_blank\">Open in new tab</a><a data-section=\"55732518\" href=\"/DownloadFile/DownloadImage.aspx?image=https://oup.silverchair-cdn.com/oup/backfile/Content_public/Journal/mnras/454/2/10.1093_mnras_stv2171/3/stv2171fig2.jpeg?Expires=1611467311&Signature=k0AUhh0Jdyl85RamcmiRWXf6ZCtFoH6nFQjh-wQM6nVRXjRP6u7JbEdZGUM0FhF8IFJoiYJhSuaGpbbgOFQJ8KLAgkDqquEXiCspJILtywhBZ-c61TX66cTEDvgMaUrlT5WLGbc8CRBVHwdfSUIkDbCHPEk1fXW0QTlOzVOQdFztcCVzg3T~yS9QV~d~ABCqJTE6Zv0MQEAPXmBIJk7os-iQyvVHC7QihDjw7y9byP0WK~QTn6LQYPBHnS964rO9CPjvhU~TsG8QGs9wrCnrZstqShHJe1D4qUcIEnJ8k-whggROS~wxrMRHB-miAENJBZ56MH7IsgymskoJA1Kmmw__&Key-Pair-Id=APKAIE5G5CRDK6RD3PGA&sec=55732518&ar=2892767&xsltPath=~/UI/app/XSLT&imagename=&siteId=5326\" class=\"download-slide\" data-path-from-xml=\"stv2171fig2.jpeg\">Download slide</a></div></div><div class=\"caption fig-caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">1D sky-subtracted spectra of DES J0115\u22125244 (left) and DES J2146\u22120047 (right). The red and blue histograms show the spectra of the two components, demonstrating that they are images of the same quasar. Emission and absorption lines are marked by blue (solid) and red (dashed) vertical lines, respectively.</p></div></div>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732519 id=\"55732519\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-1>3.1 DES J0115\u22125244</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The 1D spectra of DES J0115\u22125244 show the same broad emission lines (C <span class=\"small-caps\">iv</span>, He <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span>, C <span class=\"small-caps\">iii</span>]) at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 1.64, with a uniform ratio between the two spectra in the red, as shown in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Fig. 2</a>, indicating that the low-order differences between the two spectra are due to differential reddening, or perhaps chromatic microlensing. Together with the presence of a red galaxy in the DES images, the spectra confirm DES J0115\u22125244 as a strongly lensed quasar, with image separation \u22481.04 arcsec. Unfortunately, the S/N ratio is too low to securely detect stellar absorption lines from the deflector.</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732521 id=\"55732521\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-2>3.2 DES J2146\u22120047</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">The 1D spectra of DES J2146\u22120047 show two components with the same broad emission lines at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 2.38, consistent with the public SDSS fibre spectrum. Prominent Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> absorption lines at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.799 are detected in both spectra (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-fig2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"fig2\" data-open=\"fig2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Fig. 2</a>). The ratio between the two spectra is constant, which together with the detection of a galaxy in <em>izY</em> bands confirms DES J2146\u22120047 as a strongly lensed quasar, with image separation \u22481.32 arcsec. We associate the lens redshift with the galaxy responsible for the absorption lines at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub>. This system has been independently identified as part of the SDSS-III quasar lens sample (More et al., in preparation).</p>                    <h3 scrollto-destination=55732523 id=\"55732523\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec3-3>3.3 False positives</h3>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">Two candidates, at 20:53:56.5 \u221256:09:36 and 22:17:52.5 \u221253:57:15, respectively, are pairs of compact, star-forming galaxies. The third rejected candidate, at 22:00:24.11 +01:10:37.56, is an alignment of a <em>z</em> = 1.37 red quasar and a blue star, with the same <em>r</em> \u2212 <em>i</em> and <em>i</em> \u2212 <em>z</em> colours by coincidence.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">In general, pairs of compact star forming galaxies at <em>z</em> \u2248 0.2\u20130.3 are the main residual contaminant from the candidate-selection procedure, because their broad-band colours are consistent with those of quasars. This includes initial candidates that we rejected based on their available SDSS spectra. In <em>WISE</em> magnitudes, they tend to lie at <em>W</em>2 &gt; 14 and <em>W</em>1 \u2212 <em>W</em>2 &lt; 0.8, across the limiting locus of Assef et al. (<span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib3\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib3\" data-open=\"bib3\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2013</a>), a region that however is occupied also by spectroscopicallyconfirmed quasars and some of the candidates from this search.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732526 id=\"55732526\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec4>4 LENSING PROPERTIES</h2>\r\n<div class=\"&#xA;            block-child-p&#xA;            \">Even though the current data are not sufficient for a detailed lensing model, they can be used to derive simple properties of the lens galaxies. To this aim, we adopt a Singular Isothermal Sphere (SIS) model for the mass density profile of the deflector, which is commonly considered the simplest model apt to describe galaxy-scale lenses (Treu <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-bib31\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"bib31\" data-open=\"bib31\" class=\"link link-ref link-reveal xref-bibr\">2010</a>). The SIS projected surface density is <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ3\" content-id=\"equ3\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\Sigma (R)=\\frac{1}{2}\\Sigma _{cr}(R/R_{\\mathrm{E}})^{-1}\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(3)</span></div>with \u03a3<sub>cr</sub> = <em>c</em><sup>2</sup><em>D</em><sub>s</sub>/(4\u03c0<em>GD</em><sub>l</sub><em>D</em><sub>ls</sub>) in terms of angular diameter distances to the source (<em>D</em><sub>s</sub>), to the lens (<em>D</em><sub>l</sub>) and between lens and source (<em>D</em><sub>ls</sub>), and the Einstein radius <em>R</em><sub>E</sub> is defined such that it encloses a projected mass <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ4\" content-id=\"equ4\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\nM_{\\rm E}\\ =\\ \\pi \\Sigma _{\\rm {cr}}R_{\\mathrm{E}}^{2}\\ .\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(4)</span></div>The expected line-of-sight velocity dispersion of stars in the lens galaxy can be estimated via <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ5\" content-id=\"equ5\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\sigma ^{2}_{\\rm {sis}}=\\frac{c^{2}R_{\\mathrm{E}}D_{\\rm s}}{4\\pi D_{\\rm l}D_{\\rm {ls}}}\\ .\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(5)</span></div>Finally, neglecting microlensing, the total magnification of the point source can be estimated from the flux ratio <em>f</em><sub><em>B</em></sub>/<em>f</em><sub><em>A</em></sub> as <div class=\"formula-wrap\"><div class=\"disp-formula\" id=\"equ6\" content-id=\"equ6\"><div class=\"tex-math display-math\"> \\begin{equation}\r\n\\mu _{\\rm {tot}}=2\\frac{1+f_{B}/f_{A}}{1-f_{B}/f_{A}}\\,,\r\n\\end{equation} </div></div><span class=\"label\">(6)</span></div>where A is the brighter quasar image. Then, from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 1</a> and confirmation spectra, we can estimate <em>R</em><sub>E</sub>, <em>M</em><sub>E</sub>, \u03c3<sub>sis</sub> and \u03bc<sub>tot</sub>. The Einstein radius is approximated by half the image separation (an exact result for SIS profiles). For the flux ratio, we use the average between <em>i</em> and <em>z</em> bands, for which the photometric fit is more robust against PSF mismatch and signal-to-noise ratio(S/N), and the effects of dust and microlensing are minimized. The results are summarized in <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl2\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl2\" data-open=\"tbl2\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 2</a>. For DES J0115\u22125244, we adopted a lens redshift <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.635, which minimizes the critical surface density \u03a3<sub>cr</sub> and yields a lower bound on \u03c3<sub>sis</sub>. We also list the magnification inferred from the ratio of continua in the spectra around 6000 \u00c5. With the positional uncertainties from <span class=\"xrefLink\" id=\"jumplink-tbl1\"></span><a href=\"javascript:;\" reveal-id=\"tbl1\" data-open=\"tbl1\" class=\"link link-reveal link-table xref-fig\">Table 1</a>, the relative uncertainty on <em>R</em><sub>E</sub> is 1\u2009per\u2009cent. With current data, the uncertainties on the magnifications are of the same order as their average value.</div>                        <a id=\"55732528\" scrollto-destination=\"55732528\"></a>\r\n<div content-id=\"tbl2\" class=\"table-modal table-full-width-wrap\"><div class=\"table-wrap table-wide\"><div class=\"table-wrap-title\" id=\"tbl2\" data-id=\"tbl2\"><span class=\"label\">Table 2.</span><div class=\"caption\"><p class=\"chapter-para\">Estimated lensing parameters and properties of the lens galaxy: Einstein radius <em>R</em><sub>E</sub> (in angular units) and total magnification \u03bc<sub>tot, <em>i</em></sub> from the fit to the quasar image positions and fluxes; magnification \u03bc<sub>tot, <em>c</em></sub> on the quasar continua, from the 1D spectra; and SIS velocity dipersion \u03c3<sub>sis</sub> and enclosed mass <em>M</em><sub>E</sub> from the measured redshifts. For DES J0115\u22125244, \u03c3<sub>sis</sub> and <em>M</em><sub>E</sub> are under the hypothesis that the lens is midway between observer and source (i.e. <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.635).</p></div> href=\"/view-large/55732528\">\r\n          Open in new tab\r\n        </a></div></div></div>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732529 id=\"55732529\" class=\"section-title\" data-legacy-id=sec5>5 CONCLUSIONS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">We have presented the very first results of a campaign to extend the known samples of lensed quasars by exploiting the large footprint of wide-field photometric surveys. In particular, we have spectroscopically confirmed two new systems, found in the DES Y1A1 release with data-mining techniques. Two additional candidates were ruled out by spectroscopic observations as pairs of <em>z</em> \u2248 0.2 compact, narrow-line galaxies. Another candidate was ruled out as an alignment of a quasar and a blue star. The basic characteristics of the two confirmed systems are as follows.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>DES J0115\u22125244.</em> Consists of two images of a quasar at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 1.64 lensed by a foreground galaxy visible in the DES images. No redshift is available for the lens galaxy. The Einstein Radius is estimated to be 0.51 arcsec.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\"><em>DES J2146\u22120047.</em> Consists of two images of a quasar at <em>z</em><sub>s</sub> = 2.38, with prominent Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> absorption at <em>z</em><sub>l</sub> = 0.799, which we tentatively associate with the lens galaxy redshift. The redshift of the lensing galaxy is not confirmed in the spectroscopic follow-up by More et al. (in preparation), since detection of the Mg <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> and Fe <span class=\"small-caps\">ii</span> lines depends on S/N ratio and in fact is less evident in the worse of our two exposures, where track deconvolution becomes more noisy. Thus, deeper spectroscopic data will be needed to measure the redshift of the deflector, possibly based on stellar absorption lines. The Einstein Radius is estimated to be 0.68 arcsec.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">The main class of contaminants (including candidates rejected based on their SDSS spectra) consists of groups of compact, star-forming galaxies at <em>z</em> \u223c 0.2\u20130.3, because of their broad-band colours and compact morphology. With the observed sample, a strict cut in <em>WISE W</em>1 \u2212 <em>W</em>2 versus <em>W</em>2 would give a 100 per cent success rate, which drops at 40 per cent when the cut is relaxed. Still, with just five systems currently at hand, we would rather caution against these simple estimates.</p><p class=\"chapter-para\">Our search has delivered over 100 additional candidates from the Y1A1 data \u2013 and we expect many more from the next seasons of DES data. The results of this first follow-up effort are encouraging. However, a systematic follow-up campaign is needed to confirm large numbers of candidates, assess the purity of our selection technique, and carry out the many scientific investigations enabled by lensed quasars.</p>                    <h2 scrollto-destination=55732535 id=\"55732535\" class=\"backacknowledgements-title\" >ACKNOWLEDGMENTS</h2>\r\n<p class=\"chapter-para\">This Letter includes data gathered with the 6.5m Baade Telescopes located at Las Campanas Observatory, Chile. Images of DES J0115-5244 show a red galaxy with two blue point sources at either side, which are images of the same quasar at z<SUB>s</SUB> = 1.64 as obtained by our long-slit spectroscopic data. The Einstein radius estimated from the DES images is 0.51 arcsec. DES J2146-0047 is in the area of overlap between DES and the Sloan Digital Sky Survey (SDSS). Two blue components are visible in the DES and SDSS images. The SDSS fibre spectrum shows a quasar component at z<SUB>s</SUB> = 2.38 and absorption by Mg II and Fe II at z<SUB>l</SUB> = 0.799, which we tentatively associate with the foreground lens galaxy. Our long-slit spectra show that the blue components are resolved images of the same quasar. The Einstein radius is 0.68 arcsec, corresponding to an enclosed mass of 1.6 \u00d7 10<SUP>11</SUP> M<SUB>\u2609</SUB>. Three other candidates were observed and rejected, two being low-redshift pairs of starburst galaxies, and one being a quasar behind a blue star. These first confirmation results provide an important empirical validation of the data mining and model-based selection that is being applied to the entire DES data set.", "doi": "10.1093/mnras/stv2171", "custom1": "eprint: arXiv:1508.01203", "issn": "0035-8711", "number": "2"}, "Inspection status": "Incomplete"}
